/* Flexible box model classes */
/* Taken from Alex Russell http://infrequently.org/2009/08/css-3-progress/ */
/* This file is a compatability layer.  It allows the usage of flexible box 
model layouts accross multiple browsers, including older browsers.  The newest,
universal implementation of the flexible box model is used when available (see
`Modern browsers` comments below).  Browsers that are known to implement this 
new spec completely include:

    Firefox 28.0+
    Chrome 29.0+
    Internet Explorer 11+ 
    Opera 17.0+

Browsers not listed, including Safari, are supported via the styling under the
`Old browsers` comments below.
*/
.hbox {
  /* Old browsers */
  display: -webkit-box;
  -webkit-box-orient: horizontal;
  -webkit-box-align: stretch;
  display: -moz-box;
  -moz-box-orient: horizontal;
  -moz-box-align: stretch;
  display: box;
  box-orient: horizontal;
  box-align: stretch;
  /* Modern browsers */
  display: flex;
  flex-direction: row;
  align-items: stretch;
}
.hbox > * {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-flex: 0;
  -moz-box-flex: 0;
  box-flex: 0;
  /* Modern browsers */
  flex: none;
}
.vbox {
  /* Old browsers */
  display: -webkit-box;
  -webkit-box-orient: vertical;
  -webkit-box-align: stretch;
  display: -moz-box;
  -moz-box-orient: vertical;
  -moz-box-align: stretch;
  display: box;
  box-orient: vertical;
  box-align: stretch;
  /* Modern browsers */
  display: flex;
  flex-direction: column;
  align-items: stretch;
}
.vbox > * {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-flex: 0;
  -moz-box-flex: 0;
  box-flex: 0;
  /* Modern browsers */
  flex: none;
}
.hbox.reverse,
.vbox.reverse,
.reverse {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-direction: reverse;
  -moz-box-direction: reverse;
  box-direction: reverse;
  /* Modern browsers */
  flex-direction: row-reverse;
}
.hbox.box-flex0,
.vbox.box-flex0,
.box-flex0 {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-flex: 0;
  -moz-box-flex: 0;
  box-flex: 0;
  /* Modern browsers */
  flex: none;
  width: auto;
}
.hbox.box-flex1,
.vbox.box-flex1,
.box-flex1 {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-flex: 1;
  -moz-box-flex: 1;
  box-flex: 1;
  /* Modern browsers */
  flex: 1;
}
.hbox.box-flex,
.vbox.box-flex,
.box-flex {
  /* Old browsers */
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-flex: 1;
  -moz-box-flex: 1;
  box-flex: 1;
  /* Modern browsers */
  flex: 1;
}
.hbox.box-flex2,
.vbox.box-flex2,
.box-flex2 {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-flex: 2;
  -moz-box-flex: 2;
  box-flex: 2;
  /* Modern browsers */
  flex: 2;
}
.box-group1 {
  /*  Deprecated */
  -webkit-box-flex-group: 1;
  -moz-box-flex-group: 1;
  box-flex-group: 1;
}
.box-group2 {
  /* Deprecated */
  -webkit-box-flex-group: 2;
  -moz-box-flex-group: 2;
  box-flex-group: 2;
}
.hbox.start,
.vbox.start,
.start {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-pack: start;
  -moz-box-pack: start;
  box-pack: start;
  /* Modern browsers */
  justify-content: flex-start;
}
.hbox.end,
.vbox.end,
.end {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-pack: end;
  -moz-box-pack: end;
  box-pack: end;
  /* Modern browsers */
  justify-content: flex-end;
}
.hbox.center,
.vbox.center,
.center {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-pack: center;
  -moz-box-pack: center;
  box-pack: center;
  /* Modern browsers */
  justify-content: center;
}
.hbox.baseline,
.vbox.baseline,
.baseline {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-pack: baseline;
  -moz-box-pack: baseline;
  box-pack: baseline;
  /* Modern browsers */
  justify-content: baseline;
}
.hbox.stretch,
.vbox.stretch,
.stretch {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-pack: stretch;
  -moz-box-pack: stretch;
  box-pack: stretch;
  /* Modern browsers */
  justify-content: stretch;
}
.hbox.align-start,
.vbox.align-start,
.align-start {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-align: start;
  -moz-box-align: start;
  box-align: start;
  /* Modern browsers */
  align-items: flex-start;
}
.hbox.align-end,
.vbox.align-end,
.align-end {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-align: end;
  -moz-box-align: end;
  box-align: end;
  /* Modern browsers */
  align-items: flex-end;
}
.hbox.align-center,
.vbox.align-center,
.align-center {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-align: center;
  -moz-box-align: center;
  box-align: center;
  /* Modern browsers */
  align-items: center;
}
.hbox.align-baseline,
.vbox.align-baseline,
.align-baseline {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-align: baseline;
  -moz-box-align: baseline;
  box-align: baseline;
  /* Modern browsers */
  align-items: baseline;
}
.hbox.align-stretch,
.vbox.align-stretch,
.align-stretch {
  /* Old browsers */
  -webkit-box-align: stretch;
  -moz-box-align: stretch;
  box-align: stretch;
  /* Modern browsers */
  align-items: stretch;
}

/**
 * Primary styles
 *
 * Author: Jupyter Development Team
 */
body {
  background-color: #fff;
  /* This makes sure that the body covers the entire window and needs to
       be in a different element than the display: box in wrapper below */
  position: absolute;
  left: 0px;
  right: 0px;
  top: 0px;
  bottom: 0px;
  overflow: visible;
}
body > #header {
  /* Initially hidden to prevent FLOUC */
  display: none;
  background-color: #fff;
  /* Display over codemirror */
  position: relative;
  z-index: 100;
}
body > #header #header-container {
  padding-bottom: 5px;
  padding-top: 5px;
  box-sizing: border-box;
  -moz-box-sizing: border-box;
  -webkit-box-sizing: border-box;
}
body > #header .header-bar {
  width: 100%;
  height: 1px;
  background: #e7e7e7;
  margin-bottom: -1px;
}

.prompt {
  /* This needs to be wide enough for 3 digit prompt numbers: In[100]: */
  min-width: 14ex;
  /* This padding is tuned to match the padding on the CodeMirror editor. */
  padding: 0.4em;
  margin: 0px;
  font-family: monospace;
  text-align: right;
  /* This has to match that of the the CodeMirror class line-height below */
  line-height: 1.21429em;
  /* Don't highlight prompt number selection */
  -webkit-touch-callout: none;
  -webkit-user-select: none;
  -khtml-user-select: none;
  -moz-user-select: none;
  -ms-user-select: none;
  user-select: none;
  /* Use default cursor */
  cursor: default;
}

  }

/* The following gets added to the <head> if it is detected that the user has a
 * monospace font with inconsistent normal/bold/italic height.  See
 * notebookmain.js.  Such fonts will have keywords vertically offset with
 * respect to the rest of the text.  The user should select a better font.
 * See: https://github.com/ipython/ipython/issues/1503
 *
 * .CodeMirror span {
 *      vertical-align: bottom;
 * }
 */
.CodeMirror {
  line-height: 1.21429em;
  /* Changed from 1em to our global default */
  font-size: 14px;
  height: auto;
  /* Changed to auto to autogrow */
  background: none;
  /* Changed from white to allow our bg to show through */
}
.CodeMirror-scroll {
  /*  The CodeMirror docs are a bit fuzzy on if overflow-y should be hidden or visible.*/
  /*  We have found that if it is visible, vertical scrollbars appear with font size changes.*/
  overflow-y: hidden;
  overflow-x: auto;
}
.CodeMirror-lines {
  /* In CM2, this used to be 0.4em, but in CM3 it went to 4px. We need the em value because */
  /* we have set a different line-height and want this to scale with that. */
  padding: 0.4em;
}
.CodeMirror-linenumber {
  padding: 0 8px 0 4px;
}
.CodeMirror-gutters {
  border-bottom-left-radius: 2px;
  border-top-left-radius: 2px;
}
.CodeMirror pre {
  /* In CM3 this went to 4px from 0 in CM2. We need the 0 value because of how we size */
  /* .CodeMirror-lines */
  padding: 0;
  border: 0;
  border-radius: 0;
}

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p><a id='Sec_0'></a></p>
<h1 id="Introduction">Introduction<a class="anchor-link" href="#Introduction">&#182;</a></h1>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h4 id="Mingxin-Ye">Mingxin Ye<a class="anchor-link" href="#Mingxin-Ye">&#182;</a></h4>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p>This tutorial will will walk my audience through the entire data science pipeline, including data curation, parsing, and management,  exploratory data analysis, hypothesis testing and machine learning to provide analysis. In the dataset, we will be focusing on Admission rate, SAT admission scores and ACT admission scores and other attributes of all the universities in United States in 2015. This tutorial will start by importing the data and tidying the data. Then we will move on to analysis the clean dataset with graphics and calculations. Next step is to show our audience how to use Hypothesis Testing to test a data set. Lastly, our tutorial will go on and explain three out of four major machining learning algrithim we have learned so far. Now let's get started.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h1 id="Tutorial-Content:">Tutorial Content:<a class="anchor-link" href="#Tutorial-Content:">&#182;</a></h1><ul>
<li><p><a href="#Sec_0">Introduction</a></p>
</li>
<li><p><a href="#Sec_1">data curation, parsing, and management</a></p>
</li>
<li><p><a href="#Sec_2">Exploratory Data analysis</a></p>
</li>
<li><p><a href="#Sec_3">Hypothesis Testing</a></p>
</li>
<li><p><a href="#Sec_4">Machine Learning</a></p>
</li>
<li><p><a href="#Sec_5">Conclusion</a></p>
</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p><a id='Sec_1'></a></p>
<h1 id="Data-curation,-Parsing,-and-Management:">Data curation, Parsing, and Management:<a class="anchor-link" href="#Data-curation,-Parsing,-and-Management:">&#182;</a></h1>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p>In many cases, the dataset you are given are either very messy and hard to read, or not in a user-friendly format that is easy to analysis with. Therefore, tidy data is very important as the preperation of a dataset. Tidy data is an concept that developed by Hadley Wickham that gives people guideline of how to make data cleaning as easy and effective as possible. Here I already found a dataset that is in the format of csv which doesn't have to parsed in this case. In many other stuations, we would have to parse the data from html/text formmat to a format that are easy to use like sql or csv.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p>Before starting to import data, we need to install library: To utilize all the data analysis tools and resources, we need to install proper libraries and documentations. Pandas is a software library written for the Python programming language for data manipulation and analysis and Numpy is the fundamental package for scientific computing with Python.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[206]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">

<p>To demonstrate one type of parsing in data extraction, I decided to get dataset of the first 1000 universities in the world that is ranked by CWUR. To match the dataset above, I used the ranking for 2015.</p>

<span class="c1">#data = page.text </span>

<span class="c1">#find the table in html page</span>

<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p>With this large amount of data, it is hard to tell whether there is a direct relationship between the average SAT score
and the admission rate. Especially when the average SAT score is between 800 to 1200, the relationship seems to be random and not directly dependent on each other. However on the other side, we notice that there is a decreasing tendency when the average sat for the university go over 1200(which is usually considered as a selective/competitive score). Therefore, we decided to narrow down our data set and make a new plot with average sat scores that are higher than 1200.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>

    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">High_SAT_AVG</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">Colleges</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">Colleges</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="s1">&#39;SAT_AVG&#39;</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="o">&gt;</span> <span class="mi">1200</span><span class="p">]</span>

<span class="n">High_SAT_AVG</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">plot</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">y</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s1">&#39;ADM_RATE&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">x</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s1">&#39;SAT_AVG&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">kind</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s1">&#39;scatter&#39;</span><span class="p">)</span>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p>Interestingly with the graph above we observed a similar tendency that, with the large amount of school range, the relationship between ACT midpoint score and admission rate seems to be random and not directly dependent on each other. We also notice, above score 60, the plot starts to have a decreasing tendencyp, so we decided to make a new plot with the smaller dataset.</p>

<p>With the plot above, we observed that there is a trend that the lower the admission rate is, the higher the ACT midpoint score tends to be when the ACT midpoint score is higher than 60.</p>

<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p>Now we found a possible pattern when average SAT is above 1200 and ACT midpoint score is above 60, but not one when scores are out of those two ranges. Therefore, we wonder wether there is another factor that can come into play. I want to figure out whether it will make a difference between public schools and private schools. Therefore, I seperate data according to school type. The result is below.</p>
<h4 id="Does-school-type(public/private-nonprofit/private-for-profit)-plays-a-part-in-this?">Does school type(public/private nonprofit/private for-profit) plays a part in this?<a class="anchor-link" href="#Does-school-type(public/private-nonprofit/private-for-profit)-plays-a-part-in-this?">&#182;</a></h4>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">i</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="n">school_type</span><span class="p">:</span>
    <span class="n">Colleges_by_type</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">Colleges</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">groupby</span><span class="p">([</span><span class="s1">&#39;CONTROL&#39;</span><span class="p">])</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">get_group</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">i</span><span class="p">)</span>
    <span class="n">Colleges_by_type</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">plot</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">y</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s1">&#39;ADM_RATE&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">x</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s1">&#39;SAT_AVG&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">kind</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s1">&#39;scatter&#39;</span><span class="p">)</span>

        <span class="n">plt</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">title</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s2">&quot;Public Schools Admission Rate vs. Average Accepted SAT Score&quot;</span><span class="p">)</span>

<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">

<div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p>From the data above, we can't find a definite correlation between admission rate and Standard Test Score, but the overall trend is decreasing. With few data, we can't predict results for private for-profit schools. However, on the bright side, we did observe a more obvious decreasing trend in admission rate as the test score goes up for private non-profit schools. Which makes it more predicable for two people with same standard test score to get into a private school than a public school.</p>

<p><a id='Sec_3'></a></p>
<h1 id="Hypothesis-Testing:">Hypothesis Testing:<a class="anchor-link" href="#Hypothesis-Testing:">&#182;</a></h1>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p>What is Hypothesis Testing?
a hypothesis that is testable on the basis of observing a process that is modeled via a set of randomvariables.</p>
<p><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_hypothesis_testing">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_hypothesis_testing</a></p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p>Steps to Hypothesis Testing:</p>
<ul>
<li>Find a Null Hypothesis. It's usually the opposite of your alternative hypothesis</li>
<li>state your Null Hypothesis</li>
<li>Find a test to test your Hypothesis</li>
<li>Use the result to either reject Null Hypothesis(accept alternative hypothesis) or accept Null Hypothesis</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">

Here is the linking to a example of Statistic Hypothesis Testing using statsmodal imported from scipy:
<a href="http://knowledgetack.com/python/statsmodels/two-sample-hypothesis-testing-in-python-with-statsmodels/">http://knowledgetack.com/python/statsmodels/two-sample-hypothesis-testing-in-python-with-statsmodels/</a></p>

<h3 id="Four-majors-way-to-implement-Machine-learning:">Four majors way to implement Machine learning:<a class="anchor-link" href="#Four-majors-way-to-implement-Machine-learning:">&#182;</a></h3>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">

<ul>
<li>K-Nearest Neighbors</li>
<li>Gradient Descent</li>
<li>Decision Trees</li>
<li>Random Forests</li>
</ul>

</div>

<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">

<div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h4 id="Decision-Trees">Decision Trees<a class="anchor-link" href="#Decision-Trees">&#182;</a></h4><p>Decision Trees is a sequence of tests that very closly representation human nature of making a decisions. There are couple things needed to get it started. 
They are:</p>
<ul>
<li>a set of undecided data</li>
<li>a function h that take in data as an entry</li>
<li>the out put of the function will be a decision</li>
</ul>
<h5 id="There-are-two-type-of-notes-in-a-decision-trees:">There are two type of notes in a decision trees:<a class="anchor-link" href="#There-are-two-type-of-notes-in-a-decision-trees:">&#182;</a></h5><p>Decision node:</p>
<ul>
<li>it is the node that specify a choice or test of some attribute with 2 or more alternatives</li>
<li>every decision node is part of a path to a leaf node
Leaf node: </li>
<li>Leaf node are usually at the bottom of the tree and they serve as a classification of an example</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h4 id="K-Nearest-Neighbors">K-Nearest Neighbors<a class="anchor-link" href="#K-Nearest-Neighbors">&#182;</a></h4><p>K-Nearest Neighbors is another very funtional maching learning method.There are three things required for this method.
They are:</p>
<ul>
<li>A set of stored record</li>
<li>Distance Metricto compute distance between records</li>
<li>The value of k,which is the number of nearest neighbors to retrieve</li>
</ul>
<p>You start by finding the nearest neighbors(unknown data) to the known data(stored record) with a metric system. Then you will classify the known data with the known data. Hence unknown data become known data, so we can use those new known data to find their closest neighbours to countinue the algrorithm.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h4 id="Gradient-Descent">Gradient Descent<a class="anchor-link" href="#Gradient-Descent">&#182;</a></h4><p>Below is a basic implementation of a gradient descent algorithm. The basic idea is to find the negative of the gradient(slop) of the beginning spot, and then add the value in order to move on to the next point and calculate the negative of the gradient again to reach the next spot. The function could be used to find the local maximum.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[220]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="c1">#Problem 3 Implement the gradient descent algorithm (either batch or stochastic versions) </span>
<span class="c1">#for multiple logistic regression. I.e., modify your code in problem 1 for the logistic regression update equation.</span>

<span class="c1">#Make sure you include in your submission writeup, </span>
<span class="c1">#which version of the algorithm you are solving (stochastic or batch), </span>
<span class="c1">#and make sure to comment your code to help us understand your implementation.</span>

<span class="c1"># Training data (X, y), T time steps, alpha step</span>
<span class="k">def</span> <span class="nf">grad_descent_logreg</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">X</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">y</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">T</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">alpha</span><span class="p">):</span>
    <span class="n">m</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">n</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">X</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">shape</span> <span class="c1"># m = #examples, n = #features</span>
    <span class="n">theta</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">np</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">zeros</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">n</span><span class="p">)</span>    <span class="c1"># initialize parameters</span>
    <span class="n">f</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">np</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">zeros</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="p">)</span>        <span class="c1"># track loss over time</span>
    <span class="k">for</span> <span class="n">i</span> <span class="ow">in</span> <span class="nb">range</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="p">):</span>
        <span class="n">h</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">np</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">exp</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">X</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">dot</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">theta</span><span class="p">))</span><span class="o">/</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="o">+</span><span class="n">np</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">exp</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">X</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">dot</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">theta</span><span class="p">)))</span>
        <span class="c1"># loss for current parameter vector theta</span>
        <span class="n">f</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">i</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">np</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">log2</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="o">+</span><span class="n">np</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">exp</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">h</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">dot</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">y</span><span class="p">)))</span>
        <span class="c1"># compute steepest ascent at f(theta)</span>
        <span class="n">g</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">y</span><span class="o">-</span><span class="n">h</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">dot</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">X</span><span class="p">)</span> 
        <span class="c1"># step down the gradient</span>
        <span class="n">theta</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">theta</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">alpha</span><span class="o">*</span><span class="n">g</span>
    <span class="k">return</span> <span class="n">theta</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">f</span>
</pre></div>

</div>
</div>
</div>
